            "**Two-reader/two-author/two-critic “no bullshit” critique for Novella 1 Chapters 1–5**\n\n---\n\n### ⚙️ Reader 1 (immersive, literary reader)\n\n**What’s working**\n- The industrial-poetic voice is distinct and immersive: “friction,” “seat,” “rasp,” “cost” build a tactile philosophy that feels earned.\n- Tiffani and Jhace’s connection lands through physical gesture, not melodrama; the erotic undertone feels adult.\n- The rhythm of work—the bolts, belts, ledgers—grounds the metaphysics; it reads like labor turned scripture.\n\n**What’s not**\n- Density fatigue sets in fast. Every paragraph carries full voltage; no rest, no light/dark rhythm. Readers lose oxygen.\n- The omniscient “I’ve watched this” voice over-explains what the scenes already show.\n- Emotional variance is minimal; tone never drops below “existential grind.”\n\n**Verdict**\nGorgeous, punishing. You have Le Guin’s moral rigor with McCarthy’s grit. It needs breath—moments of silence to make the noise matter.\n\n---\n\n### 🧭 Reader 2 (story-first, casual but engaged)\n\n**Hits**\n- Opening hook works: a tired traveler, new landscape, mystery man.  \n- The four-ethic code (Fit First, Hold the Edge…) gives moral texture.  \n- Consent handled with clarity and restraint.\n\n**Misses**\n- Hard to tell when the narrator is omniscient, when it’s Tiffani’s inner thought.  \n- Supporting characters (Korv, Maelis, Lira) blur; readers can’t picture or emotionally attach.  \n- Pacing stalls—three long “let’s watch them fix machinery” sequences before plot shift.\n\n**Verdict**\nRespect, not yet love. Needs clearer stakes and a few plain-spoken emotional beats.\n\n---\n\n### ✍️ Author 1 (craft technician)\n\n**Strengths**\n- Prose control: line cadence precise, motifs disciplined.  \n- Worldbuilding via labor instead of exposition—rare and elegant.  \n- Sexual/ethical tension handled through motion and texture—mature craft.\n\n**Weaknesses**\n- Cadence sameness: semicolons and triadic phrases everywhere.  \n- “Cost?” refrain becomes tic; once per chapter would sting harder.  \n- Scene choreography repetitive—touch ↔ philosophy ↔ ledger closure.\n\n**To do**\nCut 20 % by deleting explanatory echoes. Break sentences short after heavy paragraphs to vary rhythm. Give one scene of physical rest or humor to humanize.\n\n---\n\n### 🪓 Author 2 (structure/architecture lens)\n\n**Strengths**\n- Chapters 1–5 arc cleanly: outsider → ethics → community → systemic critique.  \n- Inserted “Shift” fragments foreshadow later cosmic Audit—good spine for a sequence.\n\n**Weaknesses**\n- Stakes plateau. By Chapter 4 the friction theme repeats without escalation; Chapter 5 only restates philosophy through new scenery.  \n- The “Shift” vignettes are abrupt; need motif connection (phrasing, imagery) in the main line before arrival.\n\n**Advice**\nEither shorten to four chapters or insert an external jolt (accident, audit signal, physical failure) by mid-5 to push momentum. Let consequence, not conversation, drive the turn.\n\n---\n\n### 🧠 Critic 1 (literary/academic)\n\n**Praise**\n- The language forges a moral physics: entropy, consent, and ethics of motion.  \n- The narrator’s industrial theology is original.  \n- Consent as metaphysical geometry—bold and timely.\n\n**Critique**\n- Didactic repetition dulls the sublime. The narrator tells the reader what every scene “means.”  \n- Overreliance on rhetorical questions (“Cost?” “What else is there?”) drains force.  \n- Needs sensory grounding—smell, fatigue, cold—between abstractions.\n\n**Verdict**\nPotential modern classic of ethical-mechanical SF once pared and re-paced.\n\n---\n\n### 🧩 Critic 2 (industry/editorial)\n\n**Market reality**\n- Reads like literary-SF crossover: Le Guin × VanderMeer × Ken Liu.  \n- Boutique publishers (Tordotcom, Solaris, Apex) would look if wordcount ≤ 20k and syntax cleaned.  \n- Right now it’s 30 % too dense for general readership.\n\n**Editorial brief**\n1. Trim exposition narrator lines by half.  \n2. Re-anchor POV to Tiffani or a declared Auditor early.  \n3. Combine Korv/Lira into single composite to streamline cast.  \n4. Give one clear external plot beat by Chapter 4 (failure, injury, or audit intrusion).  \n5. Keep “Cost” refrain for chapter finales only—signature sting, not chorus.\n\n**Verdict**\nPublishable after heavy structural and tonal edit. Unique voice, needs restraint.\n\n---\n\n### 🔩 Overall Synthesis\n\n**What’s working:**  \nEthical tension embodied in machinery; sensual prose; consistent thematic spine.\n\n**What’s failing:**  \nRepetition of cadence and motif; too much narrator exposition; emotional monotone; late-arriving external stakes.\n\n**Action list**\n1. **Cut ≈ 20 %.** Target narrator asides and rhetorical “Cost?” loops.  \n2. **Insert breathing spaces.** One page of calm or humor per chapter.  \n3. **Clarify POV.** Choose: embedded Auditor or invisible chorus.  \n4. **Escalate plot by Ch 4–5.** A tangible consequence, not another discussion.  \n5. **Tonal map.** Vary sentence rhythm; allow occasional plain speech.\n\n---\n\n**Two-critic sign-off line:**  \n> “It’s brilliant metalwork—every sentence forged, every idea under tension. But the engine’s revving too high; ease the throttle, cut the commentary, and let the rasp sing for itself.”"

The pressure built in her chest, not the full cycle but a mounting clamp, like load shifting on the upper arm they'd braced the day before, threatening to test the ethics before the winter's bite.\r\nHere's where theory meets consequence—Drell's not done, the hybrid's barely inked, and the ridge farmers are isolated enough to sway. I've watched this same moment play out in valleys that held and valleys that folded. Cost? Usually decided in the next few hours.\r\nJhace's hand brushed hers as they waited, a deliberate graze that tugged warmth low, steadying the churn without words—their proximity a quiet anchor amid the assembling hands. Korv arrived first, apron still dusted from a midday wind-down, his calipers tucked away but his gaze sharp on the vendor's distant figure approaching from the main path. Lira and two other farmers joined, baskets set aside, their booklets open to the morning's entries: drought bites logged, tolls halved to ease the strain.\r\nMaelis emerged from the station house, ledger under arm, her stride purposeful as she gathered them in a loose circle by the shack. \"Hybrid's inked, but Drell's back—pushing trials on the ridge valves now, says it'll sync with network feeds. Costs waived, but we log the fit.\"\r\nKorv snorted, flipping his booklet to a blank page. \"Sync? His seals hush the stick—valve sticks, you won't feel till flood. Amputation for the hand-turn.\"\r\nDrell reached the circle then, satchel slung over shoulder, smile polished as the coastal boots he wore. \"Not amputation—precision. Sensors catch the stick before it binds, alerts to your slates. No digging floods, just data guiding the turn. Tiffani, your consult backs this? Network's reach without the rasp.\"\r\nAll eyes turned to her, the pressure spiking sharp, prick honing the circle's undercurrents: ethics clashing, choices rippling from mechanisms to lives. Jhace's fingers laced briefly with hers, hidden by the group's shift, the tug rooting courage as signals harmonized in subtle support.\r\n\"Hybrid means feels with sensors,\" she said evenly, meeting Drell's gaze. \"Not seals over noise. Ridge valves warn by rasp—log that first, or the toll adjusts wrong.\"\r\nAnd there's the line drawn—not with certs or authority, but with the honesty she learned from Korv's wind-down and Lira's frost-stuck valve. Cost of drawing it? Everything Drell promised, every smooth integration she could've stamped and walked away clean.\r\nLira nodded, graphite scratching her booklet: Vendor push: sealed valves, 15th day. Costs: trial free, but flood risk unlogged. The farmers murmured agreement, the circle tightening against the pitch.\r\nDrell's smile faltered, recalibrating. \"Risk? Data minimizes it. Maelis, think scale—ridges connect to the net, ore hauls triple without halts. Your creed: dignity in warning. Sensors warn cleaner than grind.\"\r\nMaelis drummed the ledger's edge, eyes on the upper span's cables humming faint in the breeze. \"Warnings logged true? Or averaged smooth till shear?\"\r\nThe question hung, pressure easing slightly as the group held, no cascade but contained friction. Wind-down on a sealed mock—feel the quiet lie.\"\r\nDrell hesitated, then nodded, satchel opening to reveal a small kit: bearings gleaming, sensors tiny and precise. \"Mock's fair. But results log both ways.\"\r\nThey moved to the yard's edge, where a spare springcar frame waited, its drum exposed. Jhace and Korv worked in tandem, installing the seal under Drell's guidance—minutes of precise turns, the rasp muted immediately, the mechanism whispering smooth. Tiffani watched, prick clarifying the shift: no heat bloom, no textured unwind, just sterile efficiency.\r\nThe seal here was a rubber-ringed collar, snug around the axle, trapping the grit inside until pressure built unseen; the rasp silenced to a hum, but under load, the failure brewed quiet—a sudden lock, the drum seizing without warning, frame twisting as the ore sack bursts free in a cascade of rock and snapped steel.\r\nThis is the test I've watched in a dozen valleys—the moment where the quiet's lie gets exposed or accepted. Cost? Depends on whether they're willing to see what the silence hides.\r\nThe test: wrench turned, drum releasing. Silent spin, sensors beeping alerts on Drell's slate—tension nominal, no variance. The circle leaned in, but Lira shook her head. \"Where's the edge? Flood sticks quiet till it don't.\"\r\n\"Data catches it,\" Drell insisted, but Maelis palmed the housing, brow furrowing at the cool metal.\r\n\"Run it loaded,\" she said. \"Ore weight. See the hold.\"\r\nKorv loaded a sack, the frame groaning faint under strain. The drum wound, then released—smooth at first, but a subtle bind emerged, sensors flagging late, the quiet masking the rasp's true warning. The cart jerked, coupling straining, before settling.\r\n\"See?\" Korv said, pointing to the faint crack in the frame's edge, unheeded by the beeps. \"Quiet shears without grace.\"\r\nAnd there it is—the bind that Drell's sensors caught too late, the rasp that would've warned in time sealed away in the name of progress. I've seen this same crack widen into catastrophic shear when the warning comes after the load locks. Cost? Usually measured in bodies.\r\nDrell packed the kit, smile thinning. \"Calibrate further. But the offer stands—full install, chits for cooperation.\"\r\nMaelis closed her ledger with a snap. \"Log refused. Hybrid tests on open feels first. Costs: time for mocks, 30 labor chits. Witness all.\"\r\nGraphite scratched across booklets, the circle dissolving as farmers returned to terraces, fitters to spans. Drell departed with a nod to Tiffani—\"Network'll hear of this\"—his steps clipped on the path.\r\nAlone now, Jhace turned to her, the tug pulling close as the yard emptied. \"Held the edge. The pressure released into relief, signals stabilizing intimate, consent in the shared stand. But the prick lingered, clarifying the bolt: Drell's return derailed the hybrid's ease, forcing deeper choices—ridges at risk, tolls tightening, her departure's blank field now shadowed by the quiet's creep.\r\nEvening fell as they walked the lower path, the spans' hum a rhythmic warning. Maelis's log would tally it all, but the test's jerk echoed: quiet lied, noise saved.\r\nTiffani's world had traded the rasp for smoothness, but here, the edge demanded holding—or the valley sheared.\r\nCost of holding it? They're about to find out. Drell's heading to the ridges tomorrow, and isolated farmers with drought-starved rows make easy targets for sealed progress. I've seen this play before. It doesn't end clean.\r\n\r\nChapter 7\r\nTwilight deepened over the valley as Tiffani and Jhace made their way back from the yard, the spans' cables casting faint silhouettes against the fading sky, their hum a persistent undercurrent to the evening's settling quiet. Sleep came fitful, dreams cycling through sealed drums and rasping valves, the hybrid's form refusing to seat under Drell's smooth pressure.\r\nI've spent enough nights in bunks like these, dreams grinding through the same arguments. Whatever rest you thought you'd find.\r\nDawn broke sharper than the previous, mist thick in the yard as the group assembled by the incline's base—Korv with tools, Lira and two farmers hauling a spare channel valve from the ridge stores, Maelis overseeing with ledger open. Resignation's the real thief, stealing your quiet one erasure at a time. Cost? The world's inherent grit, scrubbed or surrendered, but never silenced. In the Purist Abode's sparse, functional chamber—air clinically clean, walls bare save for a single ledger rack—Mobel the Preacher paced before his dedicated group, their chairs aligned in precise rows, his robes unadorned and pressed flat. \"The world's sickness festers in unnecessary accumulation,\" he declared, his tone edged with the fervor of one who'd tallied sins like inventory, gesturing sharply at an imagined hoard. \"Purge it aggressively; moral cleanup is the blade that carves us clean.\" The condemnation poured from him with exhausted conviction, a bone-deep drive to excise the unclean—bolstered by a faint subliminal hum threading the room, strengthening his words into unnatural clarity, as if the air itself amplified the sermon, making each syllable land like a whetstone on steel.\r\n[Eries]\r\nSurrender to the fall, though—that's the cooler lie, entropy wrapped in mercy, as if rotting means release. I've lingered in enough detunes to see how it fools you: the decay whispers insight, but it's just another rasp, temporary as rust. True quiet? It laughs from the other side. In The Detune's shadow marches, amid the counter-culture sprawl of decaying salvaged materials—beams warped from old hulls, walls patched with corroded plating that smelled of rust and damp earth—Eries the Artist sat cross-legged before her installations, chunks of dissolving metal and fabric slumped in deliberate heaps, addressing the small group clustered on crates around her. \"Decay is mercy's hand,\" she murmured, her voice low and measured, fingers trailing a fraying thread that crumbled to dust. \"Stagnation demands collapse; let it break, and form finds freedom.\" The philosophy settled in her like a settling dust, a rational acceptance of dissolution as the kindest unraveling—heightened by the strange clarity in the decaying air, a false insight sharpening her gaze on the group's attentive faces, temporary as the structures around them, already flaking at the edges.\r\n\r\nChapter 8\r\nThe ridge trail clawed upward from the valley's rim, a narrow scar of packed earth and loose scree that wound through terraced farms and scrub pine. The resonance hummed through it, relief threading deep in the balance, escalating the unspoken depth: gazes holding longer amid the rasp, touches syncing in the narrow space, pull insistent against the ethical press.\r\nDrell's shadow lingered in the margins—whispers of network reprisal, ridge yields at stake—but the bond anchored them, raw and unresolved, spanning toward the novellas' long arc.\r\nNight fell heavy in the bunkhouse, the valley's song constant through the shutters. Tiffani lay still, hand to her sternum where the forces pulsed faintly, echoing the day's grazes—the buckle, the rein, the screw. The escalation burned beneath: a friction not just of mechanisms, but of them—pulling toward an alignment that outstripped the consult, the crisis, the world below.\r\nNo words named it. But it thrummed, alive and unyielding.\r\nThe Pull thrummed relentless now, a tide eroding the Vow's edges, her palm itching to braid his tremor into hers and let the heavy chord resonate full—but Leesa's geometry demanded pause: earn the true angle, or the scar of unconsented wholeness would grind their signal into dishonest grit, moral erasure costing them the purity they'd only begun to feel.\r\nAnd that's the bind Leesa's Vow creates—the only honest friction is the one that waits for geometry to line up true. Rush it, and you scar worse than any mechanism ever could. I've seen both outcomes enough times to know: the wait either breaks you or makes the seating unshakeable. Cost? Every moment between now and then, grinding without release.\r\n\r\nChapter 10\r\nThe final bench loomed at the tower's nadir, a weathered slab of oak bolted to the foundation where the valley's deepest rasp echoed—a nexus of belt, cable, and springcar, the heart of the hybrid's first proof. Tiffani knelt by the assembly with Jhace, their hands working in tandem over the tension couplings, shims slotted precise from the ridge prototypes. The air hung thick with grease and heated metal, force cycling steady now: pressure from the network's looming shadow, pull rooting their alignment, sting clarifying each turn's fit, relief in the balance of the mechanism's song.\r\nDrell's reprisal had arrived by clerk wire that morning—sealed orders for coastal integration, yields threatened if the quiet wasn't seated—but Maelis's logs held firm, the ridge farmers' signatures anchoring the resistance.\r\nThis is the test that matters—not the mocks in the yard, but the real assembly under real load. I've watched enough hybrids fail at this stage to know: theory's easy, but metal under strain tells the truth. Cost? If this doesn't hold, everything they built on the ridge collapses.\r\nJhace torqued the final screw, his palm flat against the drum as the rasp evened into honest breath—no bind, no silence. Tiffani's hand hovered near his on the housing, the pull tugging insistent through her ribs, warming toward the contact that had steadied them through the ridge's grind. Should she? Here, now, with the logs waiting?\r\nThe question rasped brief, a hesitation grinding against the resonance's hum—professional lines blurring, the escalation too raw amid the ethical press. She let her fingers drop to the oak instead, the wood's grain biting cool under her palm, choosing distance. The force cycled on, unchanged in its balance, but the warmth ebbed faint without the bridge.\r\nJhace didn't falter, his expression steady as he wiped the housing clean, thumb grazing the rag in idle rhythm, eyes already on the next adjustment. No shift in his posture, no glance questioning the space; he rose smooth, gesturing to the cycle's even song.\r\nAnd that's the professional hold—choosing the work over the want, keeping the line clean even when the pull's grinding hard. I've seen this choice go both ways, watched some cross it and watched others hold it. Cost? The distance you maintain is the distance you feel.\r\nKorv approached from the yard, calipers in hand, Maelis trailing with the master log. \"Holds,\" he grunted, measuring the drift. \"Hybrid seats. No shear.\"\r\nMaelis nodded, graphite scratching the entry: Bench test, 17th day. Open + sensors: rasp preserved, tolerances met. Costs: 70 total mocks/labor, 30 materials chits. Witnesses: Jhace, Tiffani, Korv, ridge hands. Network reprieve logged—refused seals.\r\nThe bench-room door creaked open then, a coastal runner stepping in with a sealed dispatch tube—Authority stamp crisp, unyielding. Maelis broke the wax, her face tightening as she scanned the orders aloud. \"Junction Central. Mandating cross-pollination. Jhace's feel—proven on the bench—validates outer engineers. Continental lines, beyond the spurs. Reports in five days.\"\r\nAnd there's the cost of success—the hybrid works so well that the network wants to scale it, which means taking the one person who makes it work and sending him where the friction needs seating most. I've seen this pattern play out across every innovation that threatens the smooth line. Cost? Usually the people who built it in the first place.\r\nJhace's hand paused on the rag, thumb stilling mid-graze, but his gaze stayed even on the assembly, no flicker of surprise betrayed. Tiffani's chest cycled sharper—pressure clamping against the sudden rift, the pull twisting insistent toward him even as regret threaded faint through the professional weight. For the gap she'd chosen? Or this pull toward a world she wouldn't follow?\r\nShe swallowed it, folding the sheet precise. \"It's the seat we need—strengthens the spans.\"\r\nMaelis drummed the ledger. \"We lose Jhace's hand for rotation; we gain cover from the network.\"\r\nHe nodded once, pocketing the rag, expression unchanged—steady as the bench's song. \"Five days. Valley holds.\"\r\nNo argument, no glance her way lingering; he turned to the next crate.\r\nTiffani signed the ledger last, the blank departure field staring back—filled for him, not her, the pull unanswered as the five-day clock began its grind. The resonance thrummed on, the bond's depth escalating silent beneath the work, friction alive despite the chosen gap and the widening span.\r\nThe yard fell quiet after the runner left, the spans' hum the only sound threading through the dusk like a vein of ore waiting to be tapped. Tiffani lingered by the bench, slate in hand, tracing idle lines that mapped not mechanisms but the sudden hollow in her chest—the cost of motion pulling Jhace away, his five days a rasp against the wholeness they'd just begun to seat. She watched him work, his hands methodical on the crate, each turn a reminder of the geometry she'd withheld: the braid undone, the tide held at bay by Leesa's unyielding line.\r\nThe valley's breath surrounded her, alive with choices she'd learned to feel, but his departure loomed like a shear point, the hybrid's proof scattering into the network's vast, unfeeling flow.\r\nThe lever clicked. The rasp held. The clock ground on.\r\nAnd that's the ending you get when the friction seats honest but the geometry never lines up—the work holds, the mechanisms breathe true, but the bodies that built it move in different directions. I've watched this play out enough times to know: sometimes the cost of holding the edge is everything you wanted but couldn't reach for. Five days till he leaves. The hybrid stands. The valley breathes. And the pull between them grinds on, unanswered, like every honest friction that refuses to quiet.\r\n\r\nMeasure\r\nIt was not a room. It was a cessation of place—a hollow pause carved from the fabric of elsewhere. The sterile white aura within it held its own gravity, casting its fragile dominion across a darkness that stretched unending, dense, and absolute. Beyond that edge lay the true quiet of the universe: an absence so complete it bordered on thought.\r\nI've framed enough pauses like this one, perched on the brink where the light claims its haul but gutters out against the endless dark. Mortals etch their ledgers to cage the rasp, but this? This is the audit's manifold—where the argument gets torqued deliberate, every anomaly a shim slipped to keep the schematics grinding without locking cold. Cost? Their halts, tallied as deviations while they chase seams they think self-forged. But it hums right, that faint vibration under the brass, like the deck's rasp after a full cycle, the yield you permit to measure the strain.\r\nThe Auditor stood in the middle of that fragile light, spine straight, eyes fixed on the Calibration Console—a cathedral of brass and crystal. Cams turned like clockwork lungs. Etched glass screens shimmered with floating glyphs. Bundles of steel wire looped and twined through the manifold, pulsing faintly as friction whispered through them.\r\nShe traced one gloved fingertip across the surface, and the minute vibration sang back—measured, contained. The first-phase logs scrolled up the main crystal screen—cascading symbols tracking deviation, resistance, anomaly. Her gaze snagged on the tether line, that off-axis pull threading through the schematics: the girl, Tiffani, knotted to the fitter Jhace, her coastal certs warping the local feel into something unlogged, a distortion blooming red at the edges like heat fin scarred under unbraced load. The attachment tugged the whole manifold askew, promising cascade if not addressed—anchor or fracture, either way, it sheared the Measure's clean geometry, demanding a recalibration before the phase bled into noise uncontrolled.\r\n(She typed: Unknown interference. Crosslink forming without permission. The system compensates... slowly. Unfamiliar pattern. It bends the manifold's clean symmetry by an invisible degree. A thing that could grow. It will need to be examined. Possibly excised.)\r\nHer hands moved to the brass keys. The glyphs she typed glowed faint blue as they inscribed themselves into the logstream: The tremor is noted. Cost acceptable. The illusion of stability persists. Audit continues.\r\n\"Run the four primary schematics,\" she said aloud. Her voice carried no emotion, no echo—it was designed that way. \"Filter by integrity fracture risk.\"\r\nThe console stirred. A quiet cascade of gears engaged. The four crystalline plates lifted as one, rotating in sync like a manifold spin, light refracting into tangled models of thought and ideology—living architectures built from their makers' own contradictions.\r\nFirst rotation: Corlexi. Perfect, rigid, symmetrical lines pulsing angry crimson against the tremor.\r\n\"His rigidity compounds under stress,\" she murmured. \"When the fault line gives, the cost will be loud.\"\r\nSecond: Salee. Threads woven tight around a spindle, constricting to white-hot knot.\r\n\"Energy loss accelerating. The braid won't hold.\" Wholeness always forgets its hunger for friction. They always call stillness divine. I scribbled that in too, wrote it with my finger on the manifold's edge like something else would see it from the other side—the side of the weave where threads don't braid but bind, choking the fray they claim to heal.\r\nThird: Mobel. Pattern crackling erratic, devouring itself with fervor and fear.\r\n\"The zealot consumes the current. He'll ignite before he bends.\"\r\n(She typed: Predictable. Valuable. His collapse will feed the others' hesitation.)\r\nFourth: Eries. Lines dimming one by one, dissolving into quiet surrender.\r\n\"The still one. Always the most dangerous. They turn absence into symmetry.\"\r\nShe halted the spin, fingers returning to the manifold. She recorded the sequence: First Measure: Complete. Friction acceptable. Argument sustained.\r\nThen she pressed the obsidian stone inset in the desk. The console fell silent; the light bled from the screens until only the faint hum of internal gears remained—a heartbeat for something that didn't need to live.\r\n(The interference persists. A tether without origin. It will distort the yield if left unchecked.)\r\nShe tilted her head toward the dark that surrounded everything. For a moment, it seemed to listen.\r\n\"Now,\" she said quietly, \"we wait to see which one fails first.\"\r\nThe darkness replied with nothing—the purest kind of agreement."
